Shanghai Telephone Bureau

Progress of Automatic Switching Equipment Installation

The Ministry of Communications ordered 2 million yuan worth of telephone equipment from the American Automatic Telephone Equipment Company and ordered the replacement and installation of equipment in Nanjing, Shanghai, and Hankou. The Nanjing bureau has already completed the installation and began operation last month. Shanghai and Hankou are still in progress. According to a report by the China News Agency after inquiring with the Nanshi Telephone General Bureau, the first batch of materials allocated by the Ministry of Communications is already being installed. The switching racks inside the bureau have also been installed, with a planned number of 3,000 lines. However, the external underground cables and telephone sets have not yet been shipped. Due to the storage of the subsequent materials, special material storage yards have been built in Pudong and both the north and south city areas. However, it will still take some time before operations can begin.

First District Office of the County Holds District Affairs Meeting Yesterday

The First District Office of Shanghai County held its 13th District Affairs Meeting yesterday. Fifty village and town chiefs and others attended. District Chief Wu Jingqing presided over the meeting. After the formal opening, the following items were discussed: (1) The proposal by Beiliu Township to request that the committee in charge of the No. 25 treasury bond continue to report on the accounts. It was resolved that in addition to asking the custodian to report on the spot, the income and expenditure list should also be printed and distributed to each village and town office for review. (2) The proposal by Hancang Township to dredge the Hancang Port to benefit farmland. It was resolved to convene the relevant village chiefs to form a committee to discuss and carry out the project and to appoint the Beiliu Township chief to be responsible for convening the meeting. (3) The proposal by Pengdu Township to build the Shagang Bridge to benefit pedestrians. It was resolved that a. the bridge should be built after sufficient funds are available and b. a letter should be sent to Sima Township to effectively rectify the ferry. (4) The District Office shall print draft contracts for the sale of farmland and housing in this district in order to standardize them. The resolution was passed. (5) Confidential. (6) The proposal by Hexiangqiao Town to strictly prohibit opium and gambling. It was resolved that the villages and towns should secretly report the information to the nearby Public Security Bureau for strict investigation and suppression by the Security Corps. (7) Omitted. (8) The consensus was that the proposal by the Xiangyi Township to install telephones in Zhongdu Bridge and Hexiang Bridge should be sent to the Construction Bureau for deliberation, planning, and estimation of project material prices before being reviewed and approved. (9) The proposal by Pengku Township to prohibit sorcery. It was resolved that the village and town chiefs should report the names of the individuals and send a letter to the Public Security Bureau to prohibit the activity. (10) How to proceed with the personal registration in villages that have not yet completed it. It was resolved to complete the registration by September 15. (11) A deadline for citizens to take the oath of allegiance. It was resolved to complete it by September. (12) The proposal to widen the streets of Minhang Town was passed. (13) How to strictly urge the households to register the land at the office. It was resolved that the villages and towns should urge the households to register the land at the office. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Flexible Procedures for Members Leaving the Association

Document Submitted to the Bureau of Social Affairs: The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requests permission for flexible procedures regarding the withdrawal of fellow trade members from the association, to be decided by the executive committee and submitted to the Bureau of Social Affairs. On the 23rd of this month, a letter was received from the Silk and Satin Trade Association stating that, according to the association's charter, members who wish to withdraw must submit a written statement of reasons and obtain the approval of more than half of the members at the general meeting. However, if a member wishes to withdraw after the general meeting has just closed, or if they cease business or engage in other industries, and the investigation proves this to be true, they should be allowed to withdraw. However, as a general meeting is not easy to convene at any given time, it is asked if the executive committee can exercise its authority on behalf of the general meeting and submit it for ratification when the general meeting convenes. As the charter does not specify any basis for this, the association anticipates that such situations are inevitable for any trade association. Therefore, at the association's extraordinary meeting on August 18th, it was resolved to request an interpretation from the higher authorities. The matter is hereby formally requested to your esteemed association for an interpretation so that there is a basis for compliance. Article 7 of the association's charter states that a member's withdrawal must be approved by more than half of the members at the general meeting, which is modeled after Article 14 of the association's charter, which states that withdrawal can only occur "after being approved by the general meeting." The association's request to change this to allow the executive committee to exercise its authority on behalf of the general meeting and submit it for ratification when the general meeting convenes is because the general meeting is limited to a scheduled time, and if flexible procedures are not adopted, those who request to withdraw for legitimate reasons will not be able to do so. This is indeed a practical situation, and it is proposed that the association be allowed to amend the above clauses in its charter and request its passage when the next general meeting is convened, so that there will be a basis for handling the matter. However, before the current charter is amended, it will be difficult to handle the matter. It is reasonably requested that your bureau first issue an instruction as a decision on the matter of members' withdrawal being decided by the executive committee and submitted to the general meeting for ratification, so that the association can notify all its affiliated associations to follow suit. When the various associations convene their next general meetings, this matter can be included in the charter to make it more thorough. As the matter involves amending the charter, it exceeds the scope of interpretation, and the association does not dare to act without authorization. Whether this is appropriate is humbly submitted for your review and guidance.

Letter from Various Trade Unions in Pudong to Workers of Japanese Cotton Mills in the City

Issued in Response to the Sino-Japanese Labor Dispute

Guomin News: The various trade unions in Pudong have jointly issued a letter to workers in Japanese cotton mills in the city regarding the Sino-Japanese labor dispute. This time, our various trade unions in Pudong specially convened a meeting of representatives of various trade unions for the Sino-Japanese cotton mill labor dispute. The significance of convening this meeting is to use our united strength to assist the Sino-Japanese workers in various ways to achieve the goal of victory. The Sino-Japanese labor dispute has been going on for five weeks now. Because of the cruelty of the Japanese, it has not yet been resolved. Speaking of the origin of the labor dispute, it is truly insignificant. First, the workers made three requests to the factory: (1) Increase the rice subsidy by one dime per person per day; (2) Stop Sunday night shifts in summer; (3) No punishment for short-term work stoppages. Regarding the first article, anyone who is not blind can admit that the price of rice has indeed increased. Asking for a rice subsidy is a common practice in all factories and is by no means unique to Sino-Japanese factories. Regarding the second item, asking to stop Sunday night shifts in the sweltering summer heat is something that anyone who knows the work of a cotton mill will admit is necessary. Regarding the third item, people are made of flesh and blood, not iron. People will always have temporary illnesses or other unforeseen events, so temporary work stoppages are inevitable. However, the factory doesn't care about anything and punishes workers for any reason. The workers' requests for improvement are also fully justified and not intentionally meant to cause trouble for the Japanese. The above matters were previously approved by our national party and government agencies. Who knew that the hearts of the Japanese capitalists would be as hard as iron stones and their brains like gourds, without empathy or reason, and they would not accept them at all. One party used a small number of worker traitors and running dogs to deceive the workers. The workers could no longer bear it and had to go on strike. After the strike, the Japanese still did not realize their mistake and felt that their losses were too great, so they repeatedly wanted to start work unconditionally. The factory posted notices several times, but none of the workers went to work. Although the Japanese are thick-skinned, how can they compare to the pride of the Chinese? The Japanese took advantage of this incident to unreasonably fire seven loyal workers, saying that they were the main figures who incited the strike, which further increased the anger of all the Sino-Japanese workers. Now, the attitude of the workers is extremely calm, and everyone is thinking of giving the Japanese a lesson this time, holding the determination to fight. At the same time, our various trade unions in Pudong, seeing that the Sino-Japanese workers nearby are suffering such humiliation, naturally hold enthusiastic sympathy. We dare to say that if the Sino-Japanese workers do not win victory one day, we will do our best to help them even if we have no food to eat or clothes to wear. Our heads can be cut off, our blood can flow, but our determination to defeat the cruel Japanese capitalists will not stop for a single second. This is our attitude and determination. What are you, the workers of the Japanese cotton mills in the city, planning to do? You are suffering under the tyranny of the Japanese capitalists, just like the Sino-Japanese workers. You are all Chinese! Can you really be indifferent to the Sino-Japanese workers? You must understand that if the Chinese workers of all the Japanese cotton mills in the city unite together, the power will be amazing. If you unite and help the Sino-Japanese workers, then even the cunning Japanese will sweat and bleed white blood. We hope that you will do your best to show your support in various ways, so that the victory of the Sino-Japanese workers can be assured. The victory of the Sino-Japanese workers is also the victory of all the workers of the Japanese cotton mills in the city! Comrades, be excited! Work hard! We are willing to stand on the same front and fight to the death with the Japanese under the leadership of the Kuomintang!

Shanghai Public Security Bureau Training Patrol Leaders

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau considers patrol leaders to be the people who actually carry out duties and are responsible for supervising and directing the patrol police. On the one hand, they must also be role models. The quality of their competence is sufficient to affect the city's police administration. Most of the patrol leaders in this city are promoted from patrol police. The education of patrol police in the past was incomplete, so the competence of patrol leaders is very low. To remedy this situation, the police class taught at the training center has been temporarily suspended, and a long-term class has been established. Qualified patrol police are selected to engage in academic and technical training as a fundamental reform plan. It is reported that an order has been presented to the municipal government for approval.

Red Tanned Leather Trade Asks for Tax Reduction

Red tanned leather is a product that is very rarely produced domestically and is imported from Europe, America, and Nanyang. It is divided into three grades: high, medium, and low. High and medium grades come from Europe and America and are made by machines. The material is strong and tough, the color is bright, and the value is high. Low-grade goods are produced in Nanyang and are made purely by hand. The material is ordinary and the price is low. The artisans who make this leather are all overseas Chinese. It is estimated that there are forty to fifty leather factories in Singapore, Penang, and other places, employing no less than tens of thousands of workers. The raw cowhide material is produced in our country, shipped to Nanyang for processing, and then shipped back to the country. In recent years, domestic customs duties have increased, and the tax rate on low-grade goods from Nanyang is higher than that on high and medium-grade goods from Europe and America (omitted). The tax rate is too high, and sales have suddenly stagnated. As a result, leather factories in Nanyang have closed down one after another, and tens of thousands of workers have lost their jobs and are displaced, a very tragic situation. Only a dozen or so leather factories remain, barely maintaining a lifeline. The Chinese Consul in Singapore, to maintain the livelihood of overseas Chinese, has telegraphed the National Government to request that the import of red tanned leather from Nanyang be assessed and taxed separately according to the value of the material and that the tax rate be reduced. Therefore, the red tanned leather trade in this port also sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday requesting it to petition the Ministry of Finance for a tax reduction. The trade also hopes for assistance from all sectors.

Two Notices from the Bar Association

Types of Stamps to be Affixed

Extension of Photo Certificates

The Shanghai Bar Association yesterday issued a notice to all members, which is transcribed below: (1) Dear Sirs, we have received an instruction from the Jiangsu High Court, which reads: "For compliance with the instruction, the Ministry of Judicial Administration has instructed to notify: in the matter of the Zhejiang Tax Bureau's report that this bureau previously submitted a request in April for instructions on how to affix stamps to lawyers' certificates, etc., we were instructed to check the telegram and found that the stamp duty for lawyers' certificates is two yuan, as stipulated in the lawyers' regulations. No stamp duty is required for the register. Membership certificates should be treated as membership cases of chambers of commerce, predetermining public fees. Contracts should be charged public fees according to the example of engagement contracts. Membership fees should be treated as receipts for money. Village and neighborhood committee members, if they are documents from local autonomous organizations, should be exempted from stamp duty. We hereby notify you of this instruction," etc. In response, we have already notified all sub-bureaus to comply. Now, we have received a reply from the Hangzhou Sub-bureau stating that the President of the Hangzhou County Bar Association, Bao Xiangling, sent a letter stating that the Hangzhou Tax Bureau instructed that lawyer membership certificates should be affixed with stamps, and some were missed. The Standing Council of our association discussed this matter and unanimously agreed that lawyers and prosecutors are the three major professions in the judiciary. When prosecutors exercise their functions in litigation with the people, such as issuing receipts, they do not affix stamps. This is to respect the dignity of exercising judicial power and is truly different from lawsuits and the operations of the people. The Lawyers' Regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Justice of the National Government clearly stipulate that lawyers are performing duties, not merchants' business. Furthermore, the Zhejiang Provincial Government's 90th meeting in the 17th year of the Republic determined that lawyers are performing duties and are exempt from advertising donations. Based on this, it can be seen that merchants joining chambers of commerce and lawyers joining associations are fundamentally different. Furthermore, lawyers are appointed by parties as a litigation act, which is clearly stated in current laws and regulations. In civil litigation, lawyers' engagement and application fees are included in the litigation costs. In criminal cases, there are provisions for free defense, which cannot be compared to ordinary engagement contracts. As for the stamp duty for lawyers' certificates, it has always been paid to the ministry together with the certificate fee, so there should be no omissions. Moreover, the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Duty adopt a principle of listing items for which stamp duty should be affixed. The Central Political Conference decided that it has the nature of law, and according to the principle that orders cannot contradict laws, our association should not comply with the official letter. We hope that you will check and not feel grateful. The Hangzhou Sub-bureau stated that the case of lawyers was handled by your bureau instructing the Ministry of Finance to verify and order compliance. The association said that the order could not contradict the law and it was difficult to implement. We are now submitting a document for your review. Based on this, we have checked that the "various items" mentioned in the stamp duty regulations broadly stipulate that all receipts for money should be affixed with stamps, and do not specifically refer to receipts for money from merchants' business. When a lawyer is entrusted by a party to perform duties and obtains public fees, it is the same as the salary obtained by a public official, both of which are compensation. Salary receipts are affixed with stamps according to various receipts for money. Since lawyers are compared to prosecutors, the receipts for public fees and membership fees they issue should also be affixed with stamps. As for contracts for parties to engage lawyers to appear in court, the parties who sign the contracts should affix stamps as usual. This share of stamp duty is not borne by the lawyers' side, and the Bar Association does not need to declare its dissent. The above contracts and receipts for public fees and membership fees should not be exempted from stamps. However, your instruction that lawyer membership certificates should be affixed with stamps is a case that was approved by the Chamber of Commerce. There are no provisions for the Chamber of Commerce's membership certificates being affixed with stamps, and it is said that orders cannot change the law. We propose that your ministry add an article on various membership certificates when revising the stamp duty law to avoid excuses. The above reasons for the contracts and receipts that should be affixed with stamps are also requested to be verified and replied to the Ministry of Justice to notify the courts to comply with them in order to maintain the tax administration. The above situation in the report is hereby ordered for compliance by all bar associations under your jurisdiction.

(2) Dear Sirs, we have received the Jiangsu High Court's Instruction No. 6307, stating: "For compliance with the order to submit supplementary photos, the deadline is extended for three months," etc. We have decided to forward it to all members after a meeting of the Executive Supervisory Committee of this association. Please check and see if you have submitted supplementary photos (four photos if you are performing duties in a local court, and five photos if you are performing duties in three courts). Please submit them to the association together with your lawyer's certificate before October 20th of this year for forwarding. Late submissions will not be accepted.

Severe Banditry in Xingyang, Henan

The Henan Relief Representative Office in Shanghai sent a letter stating: "Yesterday, my old friend Zhongchuan from Henan Province escaped from Xingyang and came to Shanghai. After exchanging greetings, we talked in detail about the banditry in Xingyang. I will record it haphazardly (the following is Zhongchuan's account): The fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, and ninth districts in southern Xingyang are surrounded by mountains on three sides and have always been a place for bandits to roam. This spring, a large group of bandits occupied the northern part of Mixian County, bordering the seventh district of Xingyang, and then sneaked into Fanggu Village in the southern part of the sixth district with more than 3,000 bandits, occupying the fifth, sixth, and seventh districts, burning and looting mercilessly. It is estimated that the southern part of Xingyang, forty miles north and south and fifty miles east and west, is entirely occupied by bandits. Most of the houses in more than 500 villages in the territory have been reduced to ashes. When the stationed army of the Li Brigade came to suppress the bandits and then retreated, they pushed the captured elderly and weak into the ravines and killed the disabled on the roads. The dead and wounded were everywhere, and blood and flesh filled the mountains. The remaining fire continued to burn for three days. After investigation, more than 15,400 people were kidnapped or injured and killed, and more than 9,600 houses were burned down. The loss of property and food is even more uncountable. Now, the markets are desolate, and there are few people. Corpses are exposed and no one collects them, and the ashes of the houses are left unrescued. Those who have been kidnapped have no money to redeem themselves, and those who remain have no home to return to. This is truly a strange disaster that has never happened before." At this point, the guest burst into tears.

Huang Baiying Has Left Shanghai

She took the Empress of Canada ship to Hong Kong this morning.

The people in Wanyi Lane have left and the building is empty.

Tong Damao also went to say goodbye yesterday.

Baiying claims to embrace a single life.

Huang Baiying left Shanghai this morning. She will first go to Hong Kong and then to Singapore. The rumor that she will return directly to Guangdong is not accurate. Baiying has intended to leave Shanghai since the criminal court's verdict in the Tong Sanmao incited suicide case. According to her, it is because her family has repeatedly sent letters urging her to return to Guangdong. However, the date for the start of the appeal is set for the tenth of next month, which is only two weeks away. Her hasty departure is also quite intriguing.

Booking a Cabin Seat: Rumors of Huang Baiying Leaving Shanghai

Have been circulating for some time, but it was unexpected that she would leave before the appeal was decided. In recent days, her girlfriends have been busy preparing farewell dinners for her, and visitors to her residence in Wanyi Lane have been coming in droves day and night. Yesterday, Huang booked a cabin seat on the Changxing Company's Empress of Canada ship directly to Hong Kong at the China Travel Service on Sichuan Road. This confirmed the rumors of her departure to the south.

A Gloomy Room: Yesterday Was Baiying's Last Day in Shanghai Before Departing for Hong Kong

The reporter visited around 8 PM. Upon arrival, the reporter found that the objects in the guest room were messy, lacking its past tidiness. The photo frames hanging on the walls were also removed. The gloomy room made one feel desolate. After a while, Huang Baiying walked down the stairs from upstairs and entered the room.

Motivation for Leaving Shanghai: Huang's Face Was Fuller Than in Court

And her attitude was lively, quite different from before. The reporter asked, "Ms., is it true that you are leaving Shanghai on the Empress of Canada tomorrow morning?" Baiying replied, "Yes, it is as you say. I am going to Hong Kong tomorrow morning." As she spoke, she showed a slight surprise, but her eyes darted around, as if telling people that she felt happy and comfortable. After taking a seat, she described her motivation for leaving Shanghai, saying that she had received repeated letters from her family urging her to return to Guangdong.

Not Talking About the Lawsuit: The Reporter Was About to Ask How She Would Handle Tong Sanmao's Appeal After Leaving Shanghai

But as the doorbell rang, Tong Sanmao's elder brother, Damao, had already entered the room. Huang Baiying stood up when she saw him and invited him into the inner room. After a brief conversation, she continued to talk to the reporter, saying that after she left Shanghai, her lawsuit would be handled entirely by her lawyer and she did not want to say anything else.

Going to France: Finally, the Reporter Asked What She Would Do After Arriving in Hong Kong

To solve her future. Huang said that this matter should be reported to her

Parents' wishes will determine. However, in her heart she quite intends to study in France, and is particularly inclined to a single life. Therefore, it is difficult to say what her personal future will be for the time being. However, after leaving Shanghai, she may be able to relax a little. At this point, a porter from the China Travel Service came to move her luggage. Seeing that Huang Baiying was busy directing the servants, the reporter took his leave and withdrew.

Continued Capture of Ling Runxiang

Assassination Case Criminals

Brought to court for interrogation yesterday morning

Lu Ju has confessed to the murder

Ling's Concubine Describes the Shooting

Public Security Bureau Requests Transfer

Ling Runxiang, a native of Panyu, Guangdong, resigned from his position as detective chief of the Hongkou Police Station and was reassigned as an inspector of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. His family lived in Hongkou. On the 28th of last month, at 11 PM, Ling was having dinner with his beloved concubine, Ms. Zhang, at No. 634 Dexing Lane, North Jiangxi Road. After dinner, he took his concubine out, and as soon as they reached the entrance of the lane, they were suddenly attacked by thugs who shot him in the head. He died on the spot and the murderer escaped. Recently, the detectives of the Municipal Public Security Bureau secretly went to the Guang Wu Stage Theatre and arrested seventeen wanted criminals for interrogation. Now, the Hongkou Police Station has reported that Lu Ju, a Cantonese man, is closely related to the Ling assassination case. Lu lives at No. 789 Shunqing Lane, North Shanxi Road. At 10 AM the day before yesterday, Chinese detective Wei Jinfu, detective Feng Qi, He Chengrui, and other Western detectives went straight into Lu's room. Lu attempted to resist arrest but was bravely captured by detective Feng. A lotus-shaped pistol containing five live rounds was found under his pillow on the bed. In addition, a packet of six rounds of bullets was also seized. He was brought back to the police station for interrogation. It was learned that his accomplice, a Cantonese man named Feng Can, now lives at No. 175, Tian Road. They immediately went secretly to arrest Feng, as well as a woman named Ma Meirong and Wang Ayu. Yesterday morning, they were escorted together with the relatives of the deceased to the Special District Local Court for interrogation by Judge Feng Shide. According to Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, Lu and others are being prosecuted for murder under Articles 284, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the Criminal Code. After this case occurred, the Municipal Public Security Bureau arrested seventeen suspects. The bureau has now sent an officer to the court to request that Lu and others be transferred to the bureau for joint interrogation to determine the boundaries of jurisdiction. It is said that the incident occurred due to demands for gambling house fees, which led to the tragedy. It is said that the Cantonese vagrants in Shanghai have been given regular fees by the gambling houses. This time, Ling suddenly monopolized all the fees, so the vagrants got nothing. They hated Ling for cutting off their livelihoods, so they gathered their comrades and conspired to deal with him, vowing to eliminate Ling. Therefore, Ling was eventually assassinated. The pistol found in Lu Ju's house was the murder weapon, and Hu Ying, who is still at large, held this gun and shot Ling. The letters found in Feng Can's house also revealed a lot about the murder of Ling between the lines, and the woman Ma Meirong was Lu's mistress, and Wang Ayu was also involved with a certain man. The guns, bullets, and letters were submitted to the court, requesting that the case be postponed for further detailed investigation. Judge Feng then interrogated Lu Ju, who confessed that he had known Ling Runxiang for a long time. Since Ling monopolized all the gambling house expenses, causing everyone to be unable to withdraw money, everyone hated Ling. Therefore, Hu Ying gathered six people and decided to murder Ling, so they went together to carry out the assassination that night, but I did not go. The pistol found in my house was deposited by Hu Ying after the incident, and it was not mine, etc. I only learned of Ling's murder after reading the newspaper. The letter found in my house was written by my friend Li Bai. Li also had a share of the gambling house expenses. I don't know anything else, etc. Ma and Wang both claimed that they had not heard of the murder of Ling, and Ma also claimed that although she used to be involved with Lu, they had separated a long time ago. She had never seen the pistol in Lu's house. Then, Ling Zhang, the concubine of the deceased, said that she went out with her husband that night and suddenly heard a gunshot at the entrance of the lane, and her husband fell in response. She could still identify the person who fired the gun if she saw him. Then she chased out of the lane and saw several people running away together. Ling Junting, the cousin of the deceased, testified that my brother ordered me to buy cigarettes before leaving home. When I returned, I saw several strangers gathered in the lane, which was suspicious, so I told my brother to pay attention. Not long after, he was killed by those people. Finally, Qi Haitan, a detective from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requested that the defendants be transferred and said that Inspector Ling was under secret orders from the director on the night of the incident. Because he received an official document from the Guangdong Provincial Government that there were reactionaries coming to Shanghai from Guangdong, he was ordered to pay attention to the investigation. Unexpectedly, he was suddenly assassinated that night. The Public Security Bureau has already arrested seventeen suspects, so he requested that Lu and others be handed over to the Public Security Bureau to be brought back for joint interrogation. Judge Feng then instructed that the four people including Lu had now been prosecuted by the police station, and that they should be sentenced after interrogation. He then ordered the defendants to be taken back to prison separately and the hearing was adjourned.

Woman Covered in Needle Marks

Caused by a Barber's Gua Sha

But Died of Illness After Autopsy

In a house at No. 203 Guangxi Road, a Suzhou woman, Zhu Shunlin, was sent to Baolong Hospital by her family the day before yesterday due to illness. After the doctor's diagnosis, he could not determine her condition, but saw that she was covered in needle marks. He tentatively admitted her to the hospital for treatment. She suddenly passed away at 5 PM. The police station in charge was immediately notified (sent a detective to transport the body to the autopsy office on Feilun Road), and an investigation was launched. It was learned that the deceased was only 29 years old. She initially suffered from sha syndrome (a form of illness in traditional Chinese medicine). Her family invited Che Weikun, a barber from Suzhou who lived at No. 211 Jiangxi Road, to perform gua sha (a traditional Chinese medicine scraping technique). The needle marks on her body were caused by the gua sha. Because it was ineffective, she was sent to the hospital around 11 PM, but it was too late to save her. The barber was arrested and detained at the police station for one night. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Special District Local Court. According to Ru Baoyi, the police station's lawyer, the barber is not being prosecuted under any law for the time being, until the cause of the woman's death has been determined. However, he requested that the barber be temporarily detained pending investigation. Judge Zhou interrogated Che Weikun, who confessed that the deceased was a prostitute and her family came to ask me to perform gua sha, so I went with them. After the first needle, the patient felt a little more comfortable, but then it worsened, so I gave her another needle and asked if she had taken anything. She said she had taken opium. Her death was not due to sha, but due to drug use. Judge Zhou then ordered Che Weikun to be temporarily detained. At 10:30 AM, Prosecutor Xu, along with medical examiners, went to the autopsy office for examination and summoned witnesses for questioning. It was decided that the practice of acupuncture is a medical specialty, and how could a barber rashly perform it? He almost ruined things. Che Weikun's needles were ordered to be confiscated. As Zhu Shunlin was determined to have died of illness, the family of the deceased, Luo Zhu, was ordered to sign a certificate to claim the body for burial.

Water Supply Negotiation in Jiuruli, Zhabei

The Public Utilities Bureau Orders the Change to Tap Water

Jiuruli and Sanduoli in Yongxing Road, Zhabei, have a total of 167 houses with two artesian wells, which have been used for many years. Recently, the residents of the area, because of the insufficient amount and poor quality of the well water, jointly petitioned the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau to order the owners to switch to tap water. The bureau sent someone to investigate and found that the faucets were less than one foot above the ground, and some were even lower than the ground. When the faucets were opened, the water either dripped or did not flow at all, and the water quality was also turbid. The bureau believes that with the hot summer requiring a lot of water, the quality of the artesian wells in the area is so poor that it is a great hindrance to public health. Therefore, it ordered the owner, Dachang Company, to switch to Zhabei tap water for use before the end of August, otherwise it will be forcibly implemented in accordance with the city's water supply regulations, and the cost will be offset by the rent collected from the residents.

Superstitious Parents Send Son to His Death

Zhou Xuegeng, a Ningbo native residing at No. 175 Fuyuli, Youheng Road, Hongkou, is in his forties. His wife, He, gave birth to five sons, four of whom have died. The couple are deeply superstitious and do not like to take medicine when they are sick, often saying that they have the protection of gods and ghosts who can turn misfortune into good fortune. Unexpectedly, his third-year-old fifth son, named Guan Gen (named after Guan Yu), suffered from diarrhea and cold limbs a few days ago. He immediately asked to see a spirit medium. According to the shaman, it was his father from a previous life causing trouble, and he needed to pray to resolve it (if he asked a doctor to push away the fright, there would be no danger). Unexpectedly, yesterday at dawn, Guan Gen's face turned yellow, his breathing became rapid, and his nostrils flared. Every time he asked someone to look at the ghost, he looked at the incense head and said, "You owe him 180 yuan in your previous life, so you have repeatedly reincarnated to collect the debt. There is no hope of survival. Quickly spread a large sieve on the ground and put the child in the sieve. After death, use a knife to chop the sieve into pieces, transport the clothes and utensils you wear and burn them, and put the body in a bamboo basket and throw it into the Huangpu River to prevent reincarnation." The couple banged their heads against the wall and cried. At dawn, relatives and friends gathered and accused them of not believing in ghosts and gods and putting their son to death. They urgently asked a Western doctor to give him a life-saving injection. According to the doctor, the disease was an epidemic and there was no danger to his life, but the internal organs had been damaged due to the delay, and it was too late to save him. Before long, he died of exhaustion. The child's parents still wanted to throw the body into the Huangpu River according to the shaman's nonsense, but after persuasion from relatives and friends, they bought a coffin and buried it in a public cemetery.

Calculating Usury, Resorting to Force

Yan Hongzhang Enforces Collection by Coercion

Qin Changcai Suffers Internal Injuries

In recent years, there has been a type of vagrant in this city who specializes in lending money at exorbitant interest rates to exploit the common people. The interest rates they charge are quite different from ordinary lenders, as they stipulate that for every dollar borrowed, ten cents of silver dollars are collected daily for a period of sixteen days. If the interest is lacking or the principal and interest cannot be repaid on time, they have methods to deal with it. They will immediately gather accomplices and resort to coercion. If there is any hesitation, they will be subjected to brutal beatings, hence the name "fist money." It is said that even a slight shortage results in a fist to the face. Those involved in economic relationships, even if they know the danger, once they try it and are unable to cope, they will be met with brutality, causing great harm. A man named Yan Hongzhang from Jingjiang, residing at No. 24 Diandang Lane in Nanshi, engages in this business while also selling fruit. Previously, Qin, brother of Qin Changwen from Haimen, who pulls rickshaws at Wuzhua Lane in Nanmatou, borrowed one dollar of fist money from Yan due to urgent needs. Yesterday was the deadline, and he had no way to repay it. Yan immediately gathered Li Wenshan and others to demand payment. Coincidentally, Qin's brother was out, so they coerced Qin Changwen in various ways. A disagreement arose, and a major conflict erupted. Qin Changwen was punched and kicked, resulting in internal injuries. He collapsed in extreme pain and lost consciousness. Ma Yunlong, the watchman of the 31st post in the area, heard the commotion and arrived, taking the group back to the relevant branch of the First District. Afterwards, the branch chief received an anonymous letter stating that Yan and others had a notorious record of wrongdoing and were pests of society, requesting severe punishment. As the matter concerned injury, he immediately prepared a document to be transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for interrogation.

Hooligans Demand Extortion, Resort to Violence

Hu Wenhui Suffers Six Axe Wounds

Hu Wenhui, a local residing at No. 748 Xidexin Lane, Peng Road, Hongkou, who is over thirty years old, has been working as an inspector at the Dadong Dance Hall. Yesterday evening, around 7 PM, while playing mahjong at a friend's house at No. 147 in the same lane, three hooligans came, claiming that the homeowner was running a gambling den and demanded five yuan. The three hooligans, upon hearing this, were quite dissatisfied with Hu, considering him to have overstepped his bounds. The head wound was the most severe, cutting about an inch deep and exposing the skull, with blood flowing all over. However, Wenhui was young and strong. Despite his severe injuries, he managed to seize an axe from the hooligans. Seeing that their extortion attempt had failed, the perpetrators scattered and fled out the door. Hu was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Subsequently, the hospital reported the incident to the Hongkou Police Station, which launched an investigation to apprehend the perpetrators and punish them.

Boarding Master Assaults Female Worker

Recently, in the vicinity of Shanghai West, the business of boarding masters who exclusively provide meals and lodging for female workers in yarn factories has been on the rise. Most of the female workers in these boarding establishments are recruited by the masters from various counties in Jiangbei. Each female worker is given a settlement fee of 30 yuan, with the understanding that they will work for three years. After bringing them to Shanghai, the master introduces the women to work in factories, and all wages earned each month are pocketed by the master. Furthermore, they are often treated very cruelly, leading to frequent disputes and quarrels between the masters and the women. Around 7 PM on the afternoon of the previous day, Zhu Mangkou, a 17-year-old woman from Taizhou, who resides at Chen Jinchu's boarding establishment at No. 96, Building 1, of Xihe Garment Factory on Robert Road in Shanghai West, has been working at the Xihe Yarn Factory. Because she has been abused by Chen recently and has been staying at Chen's boarding house for a long time, her wages have been swallowed up by Chen. The woman realized her predicament and decided to break away from Chen. Fortunately, female workers from the same factory saw the incident and alerted the police, who arrested both Chen and his wife and brought them back to the Sixth District Police Station. After District Chief Ren interrogated them separately, as the case involved forced female labor and assault, he immediately prepared a document to be transferred to the Local Court for interrogation.

Dai Jinrong Beaten to Death by Coolie

The Result of a Dispute Over Moving a Hemp Bag

Dai Jinrong, a coolie who carries cotton flowers at the Housheng Yarn Factory at No. 22 Lan Road, was carrying flower clothes on the bank of the factory's river at ten o'clock in the morning when someone on a sailing boat in the river placed two bags of cotton on the shore, obstructing Dai's passage. Dai asked Tao Fuxiang, the boatman, to take the bags back onto the boat, but Tao refused. A dispute ensued, which then escalated into violence. Chen Fukuan, Zhou Yushu, Ma Er, and Tao Fujin, all from the boat, stepped forward to help Tao beat Dai with a rain of fists, many of which hit vital points. Dai was immediately injured and killed. Pan Yulin, Zhang Yunjian, and other detectives from the Yangshupu Police Station went to the scene and arrested Tao and the other four, pending transfer to the court for interrogation. The body was sent to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Xu Mei, a prosecutor from the Special District Court, led a forensic doctor and others to the office to examine the body and determine the cause of death. According to the report of the Deputy Detective from the West, the five suspects stated that they were denying many aspects of the case, while the Chief Detective from the Police Station stated that he needed to prosecute the five suspects. Mr. Xu then questioned the wife of the deceased and, after further examination, ordered the body to be handed over to the wife of the deceased for burial, and the five suspects were to be prosecuted by the police station pending interrogation by the court.

Accusation Against County Tax Collector Cheng Gentang

Cheng Gentang, a tax collector of the Shanghai County Finance Bureau, fabricated facts and misled his superiors, resulting in a joint petition from the heads and deputy heads of various townships in the First District to the First District Public Office, requesting that the county government dismiss him from his position and punish him as a warning against cunning. The original petition is transcribed below: The petition is regarding a cunning official fabricating charges, humbly requesting that the county government dismiss and punish him. Since we township heads have received the clear order to collect the overdue winter grain tax from the 18th year of the Republic, we have repeatedly urged payment and dared not neglect our duties. However, due to successive years of poor harvests and the continued increase in the cost of living, diligent work throughout the year is still not enough to fully meet the needs of supporting families. There are indeed many households in each township that are behind on payments, but they are all forced by circumstances and cannot be equated with those who deliberately resist. This summer, heaven was unkind again, and a sudden disaster struck, destroying almost all crops, making the livelihood of the common people even more difficult. At this time, if we were to drain the pond to catch all the fish, it is conceivable that they would take risks and face even greater difficulties in the future. We have jointly petitioned Your Excellency to request an extension of the deadline, so that the collection of taxes also includes an intention to appease. Such a method, we believe, is beneficial to both public and private interests. Unexpectedly, the tax collector Cheng Gentang, harboring suspicion of insufficient supply, fabricated accusations, claiming that we gathered crowds to resist the grain tax and begged the district chief to reason with us, which we ignored, and reported this to his superiors. We know that grain transport is an important source of revenue for the country, so how could we collude to resist it? If any of the allegations made by the official are true, then the law is in place and we cannot avoid punishment. However, if he fabricated the accusations, then it is a matter of slander and he should be punished in turn. Therefore, we humbly implore Your Excellency to request that the county government order the relevant authorities to swiftly dismiss and punish the official as a warning against cunning and to reassure the good and kind, which would be a meritorious act.

Electric Shock Death at Tuberculosis Sanatorium Outlet

Wu Tianfeng, who ran an outlet shop at No. 33 Bazilu Road, Shanghai Tuberculosis Sanatorium branch, sneaked into the X-ray room at 9 AM yesterday morning. While playing with the X-ray equipment, he accidentally received an electric shock and died. Someone entered and discovered the incident, reporting it to the Hongkou Police Station, which instructed detectives Shen Dehui and others to investigate. The report was true. The body was taken to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Xu Mei, a prosecutor from the Special District Court, visited the office to examine the body. According to the report of the Deputy Detective from the West, Wu Tianlong, the brother of the deceased, stated that the deceased was his brother and that the body could be handed over to him for collection. Prosecutor Xu then ordered the body to be handed over to Wu Tianlong, the brother of the deceased, for burial.

Verification of Ma A'lai's Death by Robbery

Ma A'lai, a native of Shaoxing who lived at No. 179 Guoging Road, Zhabei, and worked as a ash collector, went to the French Concession on the previous morning to collect outstanding accounts on the Pi Shao Nai Road. At 11:00 AM, he went to his friend Chen Jifu's place on the third floor of No. 287 Xixinqiao Street to rest. Suddenly, two bandits rushed upstairs to rob him, but failed. They opened fire with a handgun, and a bullet hit Ma's right abdomen. The bandits took advantage of the situation to escape. Chen reported the incident to the police, who sent Ma to Renji Hospital. He died in the hospital at 3:00 PM due to his injuries. The hospital notified the police, who took the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang Forensic Examination Office to await verification. In the morning, the Criminal Division of the French Concession Police Department summoned the deceased's wife, Ma Disi, and the witness, Chen Jifu, to the court. According to the Chief Detective's report, Judge Zhu questioned the deceased's wife and the witness. He then ordered that the examination confirmed that the deceased Ma A'lai had died from a gunshot wound sustained during his lifetime. Photographs should be taken, and the family of the deceased was permitted to collect the body for burial. The police were to apprehend the perpetrators for investigation.

News from Various Trade Guilds

Tea Industry: After the formal establishment of the Tea Trade Association, the first executive committee meeting was held yesterday. More than a dozen executive committee members attended the meeting, which began at 3:00 PM. Mr. Yang Shangting was elected as the chairman. After the formalities were completed, the following was discussed: Regarding the case where the Workers' Union repeatedly sent letters requesting an increase in the wages of workers, it was resolved that, regardless of the rank, each worker would receive a monthly salary increase of two yuan starting from September. The association will notify all members of the industry in the city to follow suit. If any increase has been automatically granted this year, the amount added should be calculated accordingly. Regarding the case of reorganizing industry regulations, it was resolved that all industry regulations previously approved by the government, whether or not they were members, must be strictly observed and that private scales, price reductions, and other destructive acts are prohibited. Otherwise, according to the registration, the original charter will be enforced. Regarding the case where members are not allowed to withdraw from the association without reason, it was resolved that members who wish to withdraw from the association must follow Article 7 of Chapter 2 of the association's constitution and state the reasons for withdrawal in writing before further processing. If they resist contributions without reason, their names will be published in the newspaper to announce their removal and cancellation of their qualifications as legitimate merchants, and they will no longer be protected. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Sauce and Liquor Industry: The Sauce and Liquor Association held its third executive committee meeting on the afternoon of August 24th. All members were present. Chairman Zhang Dalian discussed the following items: (1) Regarding the White Liquor Inspection Office's decision to implement the joint police and arrest inspection of liquor unloading and stamp verification starting from September 1st, it was commonly stated that applying stamps after unloading has the disadvantage of taxing goods multiple times, and joint police and arrest inspections have the suspicion of imposing excessive taxes and disturbing merchants. It was resolved to send a letter of objection and to contact the relevant associations to proceed together. (2) Regarding the case of setting a date for signing a draft agreement with the Workers' Union, due to the petition of the Workers' Union published in the Shenxin newspapers today, the Social Bureau instructed that problems between workers and clerks should be resolved through negotiation. It was resolved to send a letter to the Workers' Union to postpone the signing. (3) Regarding the case where the salaries of managers of various businesses in the industry should be appropriately increased, it was resolved that the standard salary for managers should be between 20 and 25 yuan. If the salary exceeds the standard, there are no restrictions. (4) Regarding the case of illegal cargo detention by the Shaoxing Wine Association, it was resolved to reach a settlement within three days; otherwise, separate reports would be submitted to various agencies in Beijing and Shanghai for thorough investigation. (5) Regarding the case of rewarding lawyers after settling a lawsuit with the Workers' Union, it was resolved to pass the proposal. (6) Regarding the case where the association staff requested a salary increase, it was resolved to temporarily add two yuan. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Sea Guest

A (with his friend B in a restaurant after finishing their meal) — This waiter is so rude. I gave him half a dollar as a tip, and he didn't even say thank you.

B — If you didn't give him anything, see what he would do.

Waiter (hearing their conversation, turns around) — Sir, we have our rules. If the tip given by the guests is less than one dollar, we can only give a look of attention to indicate receipt. Only when we get a full dollar do we say thank you.

Mother — Child, are you fighting again? How did you lose two front teeth?

Child — Mother, I didn't lose them. I've wrapped them up and hidden them in the drawer.

Ship's Officer — Madam, I have instructed the waiters to serve you with special care. Why are you still dissatisfied? What exactly do you want?

Seasick Woman — I — I want a piece of land.

Procurement Officer — Is this horse any good?

Horse Trader — Couldn't be better. It's a real warhorse. Perfect for the front lines.

Procurement Officer (after trying to ride it) — Damn it, damn it. You dare to deceive me. This horse can't run fast at all. You still call it a real warhorse?

Horse Trader — Why not? Soldiers should rather die than run away, shouldn't they? This horse would rather die than run too. That's why I say it's a real warhorse.

My Observations on This Year's National Day

— Shen Hengzhuang

A strong nation. Great citizens. Regarding the National Day of their motherland, they invariably make us clearly see their fervor and various forms of exciting revelry. The French celebration of their democratic anniversary is one such example.

But looking back at our China, for the great commemoration of National Day, aside from the rigid commemorative gatherings convened by the authorities, grand celebrations spontaneously organized by the people are simply non-existent. This cannot help but allow other strong nations to secretly laugh at our citizens' lack of national consciousness, and we ourselves cannot help but appear weak to the outside world.

Now, the great commemoration of National Day is about to arrive in an instant. If the citizens remain so indifferent, one ultimately feels a bit ashamed towards Mr. Sun Zhongshan, the founder of the nation. However, amidst this silent attitude, I heard exciting news, that is, for this year's National Day, many new figures in Shanghai's business circles and young people in social circles are preparing to unite and hold a grand celebration, preparing to compete with France and other strong nations. I heard the venue has already been booked at the Dahua Hotel. It is expected that on that day, there will surely be many enthusiastic individuals, taking advantage of the fervent mood, indulging under the sounds of music.

A Tragedy of a Fatal Word

— Chen Boying

Lu Xingkun, a doctor in Henghe, Yuyao, initially had no great reputation. In recent years, his medical practice has been thriving, and people from far and near have flocked to him. Every second, fifth, and eighth day of the month, he would go to Xiaoqiaotou for consultations, a place thirty miles from Henghe. One day in the late part of last month, Lu was invited to Guanhaiwei by someone surnamed Mou for a consultation. Upon returning, it was already late. Lu always took his own pedal boat. That day was no different. As the boat was traveling near the Taiping Bridge close to the Ganlu Temple, someone on the shore asked, "Is that boat carrying Dr. Lu?" The boatman replied, "Yes." The person said, "Then stop for a moment." Before the boatman could respond, the person on the shore had already jumped into the boat. There were three of them, each holding a handgun. They entered the boat and immediately searched Lu's bag, finding more than ten yuan, which they took. They also took the long gown Lu was wearing. Lu was angered and said to them, "Don't do this! I recognize you!" Upon hearing this, the robbers were both angry and alarmed. They immediately shot Lu, piercing his chest. The robbers ransacked everything in the boat and fled. The boatman was extremely frightened and could not make a sound. He wanted to take Lu home for treatment, but Lu died before they had gone half a mile. The boatman then reported to the authorities and told them what had happened. Alas! In ancient times, there was the saying "three words can make a rafter," but Lu lost his life with a single word. How unfortunate! However, robbers are all desperate criminals. They have forgotten their own lives, so how can they care about the lives of others? If Lu had been a little more patient and pretended to be deaf and dumb for a moment, how could he have lost his life to a bullet? As the saying goes, "The mouth can stir up trouble." This is truly not a false statement. It is said that the murderers have already been apprehended. This shows that robbery is both something that can and cannot be done.

World Buddhist Academy Under Construction in India

— Lai

Letter to Master Taixu of the Wuchang Buddhist Academy: Revered Taixu, the earliest place where the Buddha transmitted the Dharma was formerly called Risipatana (i.e., Deer Park), now called Sarnath. The Manohara Vihara Temple being built here by your disciples will soon be completed. We hereby report this. Your disciples plan to complete it in October and intend to invite the King of Siam to hold the consecration ceremony. The construction of the World Buddhist Academy is only one aspect of it. We are deeply aware of this. Your disciples plan to invite students from various Buddhist countries around the world, as well as those who know Pali and Sanskrit, to come and study Buddhism. We hope you will provide us with a list of names and addresses of famous Chinese monks and scholars so that we can invite them to participate. If our master can come, we will set up a reception area for the master and a Chinese reception area. The chairman of our association, Dhammadharānanda, sends his regards. This is to inform you. We wish you all the best.

China's Talking Pictures

— Beigong

A few months ago, I was moved by the alluring advertisement of a cinema, which said "Premiering a domestically produced talking picture." I rushed to see it, but could not help but be disappointed. It was still a silent film, but with two live people repeating the words spoken by the actors in the film. This matter was truly ridiculous. It is said that at the time, the Film Censorship Board, because of its confusing intent, had sent a letter of warning. Now, it has indeed disappeared. But from this, I felt that the timely emergence of a real Chinese talking picture is a must.

Taking Shanghai as an example, the amount of Chinese money that flows out to foreign countries through foreign films is very, very large. Since the prevalence of talking pictures, the number has become even more alarming. Chinese people are simply amazed by its novelty and are accustomed to being fashionable, and they flock to it. However, I am afraid that very few people can clearly understand the conversations in foreign talking pictures. Even if we put aside the loss of money, in terms of the audience's enjoyment, it always feels like it is reduced a lot.

If China could create its own real talking pictures, there would be at least two benefits: First, take this opportunity to restore the Chinese people's faith in domestically produced films. Second, Chinese people will naturally find domestically produced talking pictures more intimate and enjoyable. Therefore, it could strike a blow to foreign talking pictures.

Not long ago, it was rumored that the Star Film Company had decided to create talking pictures. Each one has been tested and verified and has indeed achieved satisfactory results. It is definitely not a kind of speculation of a slippery nature. It is said that the first film has been named "Sing-Song Girl Red Peony." From this, it seems that a new glorious page has been added to the history of Chinese cinema. And the eight characters "Complete singing and dancing, complete dialogue" will no longer be the exclusive domain of foreign films.

Judging from the facts, this is indeed the best opportunity for the revival of our country's film industry. Then I hope that the Star Film Company will be particularly cautious and careful with this first talking picture. Because the future life of the declining film industry depends entirely on this talking picture. Come on! I also hope that the Star Film Company can publish the production process so that we can know some of their efforts and achievements.

A Record of Qu Shangyu Cutting Flesh to Treat His Father

— Jiang Shoushi

Cutting flesh [from one's body for medicine] is ignorant filial piety. Those with knowledge criticize it. However, in this world of turbulent seas, how many people can perform such ignorant acts of filial piety? Therefore, one cannot but praise Shangyu's filial piety and its ignorance. Shangyu, surnamed Qu, is a native of Haiwu. He is fond of learning and deep thinking and rarely speaks or smiles with others. He is fond of drinking. After getting drunk, he would talk about everything. He is truly a man of temperament. He is skilled in painting. He earns a living in Shanghai and has a very good reputation. His venerable father, Mr. Jingcai, is an experienced and respected man. He is the third child in his family. People respectfully call him Mr. San [Third Mr.]. He was working in the provincial capital and returned home early due to illness. Shangyu also rushed to his side, but Mr. San's illness was already critical. Shangyu was saddened and thought that there was no way to treat his father, so he imitated the act of cutting flesh. He hoped to move Heaven. Late at night, he dismissed everyone, set up an incense table, and prayed. After praying, he cut his arm with sharp scissors. There was a shivering sound. The wound was like a cup, and the blood was wet but did not flow. He rushed to the stove and threw the flesh into the pot. A cool breeze suddenly came. The fire in the stove flickered. As it was about to boil, the flesh suddenly leaped out. He threw it in again. It was like before. He threw it in a third time, and it finally stayed. Then he held the soup and went forward. At that time, Mr. San was still conscious. After drinking it, he felt something different. He sternly questioned him, and Shangyu finally told the truth. They cried together loudly. Two days later, Mr. San died. I have been friends with Shangyu for a long time and know his character well. His reason for doing this was to seek peace of mind. He did not know about filial piety, let alone whether his filial piety was ignorant or not. But the world will surely attribute filial piety to him. Is that what he wants? Mr. San's elder brother, named Yinzhou, was devastated upon hearing the news. The filial piety and fraternity of the family showed that Shangyu's inherent qualities had a source. Alas! It is all touching.

An Analysis of the Recent German Political Turmoil (Part 1)

— Li Liuzeng, sent from Paris

The German political situation has gone from crisis to stability, and from stability back to crisis. The results of its changes often exceed people's expectations. Since Dietriech succeeded Moldenhauer as finance minister, we thought that Bruning's cabinet had a thicker power base and could stabilize things for a while. Unexpectedly, since last week, due to general affairs issues, the government and parliament went to extremes, holding each other for ten days without being able to compromise. Now, it is rumored that the government has dissolved the parliament.

Although the appearance of this incident is different from before, when viewed from the inside, it still has its consistency. The dispute between the government and parliament is always about financial issues. The dismissal of former Finance Minister Moldenhauer was because he wanted to impose a kind of sacrifice tax on the people. Now, Dietriech has encountered the same difficulties in parliament with the same issue. But this time, the cabinet's attitude is tough. Prime Minister Bruning has been fully authorized by President Hindenburg to overcome all difficulties in order to implement his policies. Thus, the parliament, which has always obstructed government policies, was finally dissolved. I will briefly explain the course of events.

Recently, due to insufficient national funds, the German government, on the recommendation of Finance Minister Dietriech, proposed to increase income tax and single tax by 5% in order to remedy the situation. However, this proposal was rejected by the parliamentary treasury committee on the 12th of this month by a vote of 15 to 13. At that time, the finance minister, seeing that the situation was unfavorable in the committee, declared that the original proposal would no longer be reviewed by the committee and would be submitted directly to parliament for a public vote.

After two days of verbal warfare, on the 16th, parliament again voted 256 to 204 to reject the government's proposal. However, on the same day, President Hindenburg had authorized cabinet prime minister Bruning to issue new tax bills by government order in accordance with Article 48 of the constitution when necessary, or even dissolve the parliament. Therefore, that evening, Prime Minister Bruning issued several orders, levying a 2.5% sacrifice tax on those with an annual salary income of more than 2,000 marks, a 5% supplementary income tax on those with an annual income of more than 8,000 marks, and a 10% single tax on unmarried men and women with an annual income of more than 2,640 marks.

After the government orders were issued, the Social Democratic Party immediately proposed a motion to repeal the government orders. The results of the vote on the 18th were that the motion to repeal the government orders was passed. Thus, the government had no way to go and had to announce the dissolution of parliament.

This time, Prime Minister Bruning resolutely dissolved parliament because he had the trust of President Hindenburg. Although this inevitably has the suspicion of dictatorship in politics, it was also a last resort. Because the cabinet had no possibility of uniting a majority in parliament, and the financial policy set was necessary for the present and future of Germany. Moreover, from the perspective of the German national position, the observation is the same as from the international position. Dissolving parliament and holding new elections may be better than cooperating with the right wing, which is entirely controlled by Hugenberg. (Before the parliamentary vote, Hugenberg contacted the government in his capacity as the leader of the right wing. Because the conditions he put forward were harsh and not accepted by the cabinet, he voted against it.

Warmth in the Heart (262)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Thirteen: Who Unintentionally Gains a Jade Ring by Sowing Good Fortune? Only This Karma Inspires Songs of Golden Threads

After Channong was seated, Zuo Shichen said to her, "I didn't know you were out. It was only when Aba, who's with Zuo Cuiyun, mentioned it just now that I found out." Channong smiled faintly. Zuo Shichen felt very sad seeing her smile. The smile clearly didn't come from the heart, and it contained an indescribable bitterness. It was a kind of bitter smile. The two were silent for a while. Channong took the powder paper from the back of a small golden mirror and dabbed it on her nose. Then she said, "Second Young Master, we haven't seen each other for three or four years. How do you think I've aged? Tell me honestly." Zuo Shichen really wanted to say that she had indeed aged a lot. But looking at Channong's pitiful appearance, he had to make a disingenuous remark and said, "Not at all. You're still the same as before." Channong smiled sadly again and said, "Still the same as before? I know myself that I've aged a lot." Zuo Shichen didn't want to hear her continue, so he cut her off and said, "Look, I've aged quite a bit too." Channong said, "You don't look old at all. You're really the same as before. What does it matter if a man ages a little? When we women age, our lives are over." Zuo Shichen said, "Why did you come out again?" Channong said, "You've scattered here. Come to my business. This can't be explained in two or three sentences. Besides, it's not good to talk about it in this place now." Zuo Shichen said, "Today I'm being a host reluctantly. I'm afraid the party won't end early." Channong said, "Then come tomorrow. Come earlier tomorrow. If you want to talk about my affairs, it would take two or three hours. If you were to write a novel, it could be a thick book. Anyway, I have few performances now. Come to my place for supper. The place is in Baihuadi. Baihuadi is the only teahouse we have now." Zuo Shichen thought that he had indeed never been to Baihuadi. He once made a riddle. The riddle was a line of poetry: "When the last cherry blossoms fall, the spring is over." The answer was a place name in Shanghai: "Baihuadi" [Bottom of a Hundred Flowers]. Because of this riddle, he thought of Cuiyun's past years, truly like flowing water. It had reached the end of spring. The bright and colorful time was like a fleeting glance without a trace. She lived in Baihuadi. She really wanted to complain to the God of Spring about the lateness of twilight. Turning back to look at Channong, although she smiled with her head lowered, the wrinkles naturally appeared on her eyebrows and the corners of her eyes in the smile. It was no longer something that could be covered up by the power of rouge and powder. The twilight of middle age suddenly drilled into her blood and could no longer be cleared away. It was probably imaginable what kind of suffering she had endured in the three or four years since she got married. Because although she was a quiet girl, she used to have delicate and distant criticism. But now, it seemed that her lively mood had been gnawed away by the decadent environment.

Dongxin and Beishi are similar, and the transformation of Yuan rice is happening, and the price is also weak, as well.

Wuhu New Guest Indica Rice Has Arrived in Shanghai

Yesterday, the Yangmi market initially showed signs of weakness, but then inland traders purchased mid-grade goods. Tianjin traders also bought one boat of Saigon rice with 1,000 bags. The market then stabilized. In the afternoon, there were continuing inquiries from inland villages, and the market seemed stable. The opening prices were 1,500 bags of Saigon rice, priced at 16.02 yuan to 15.35 yuan; 500 bags of Grade 2 rice, priced at 13.75 yuan; 500 bags of Big Broken rice, priced at 12.5 yuan to 11.8 yuan; 100 bags of Small Broken rice, priced at 14.5 yuan; and 100 bags of Cover Rice, priced at 15.25 yuan.

Guest Indica rice from all regions has entered the market. The harvest in Hunan is the best. Wuhu and Jiangxi are also better than last year. Wuhu is closer to Shanghai. The first batch of new rice has already been loaded and arrived, with 246 bags priced at 11.67 yuan, or 11.8 yuan including commission. It is said that it was purchased by Tianjin traders.

Standard Flour Market Is Very Good

After the opening of the flour market yesterday, there were short covering in the current month's futures contracts, and the market was very good. The opening price was 2.5725 taels. Factories were unwilling to deliver spot flour due to low inventory, and traders from the north and south oceans were preparing to purchase warehouse receipts. The market became more stable. Forward months were very weak in the morning, and there was no buying or selling. In the afternoon, Yang flour and wheat became tight due to the large movement in the gold market. Customers who were selling were also covering their positions, and the market was more active than the current month. At the close, the current month was up 0.01 tael, next month was up 0.005 tael, October, November, and December were up 0.0125 tael, and January was up 0.0175 tael.

Near-Term Wheat Suddenly Rises by 0.05 Taels

After the opening of the wheat market yesterday, prices for all months were surprisingly active. This was still due to the rise in foreign wheat, few arrivals of spot wheat, and market sentiment being bullish. Customers continued to hedge forward months, which were slightly soft. The current month was driven up by high-quality factories competing for scarce spot wheat, and shorts dared not sell further due to the impending delivery date. Prices gradually rose, and the closing price was up 0.05 taels. September and October were up 0.02 taels each, and November, December, and January were up 0.03 taels each. Only medium-quality and low-quality goods arrived for spot wheat, and high-quality goods were scarce. Factories were very interested, so the price rose another 0.05 taels. More than 4,000 bags of various brands were sold, divided among various factories.

North-South Goods: Zhangzhou and Tong'an Longan Simultaneously Launch New Products

The longan produced in Zhangzhou and Tong'an has a good harvest this year. The Taikoo Company's Jinan wheel from Xiamen brought the first batch of new goods from Zhangzhou and Tong'an. All sizes of goods were available. The initial market will definitely be stable and active. The opening price can be expected today or tomorrow. Guangdong goods arrived a few days ago, but they were small and medium grains, and the market was ordinary. Quanzhou bubble longan will arrive in ten days, while Xinghua longan will take another twenty days. This year's harvest in various places is considerable. The market is expected to gradually loosen in the future.

Silk and Tea: New York Raw Silk Prices Plunge

Factory Sales Stagnate... Prices Plunge by 0.2-0.3 Dollars

In the New York market, silk consumption has decreased significantly due to the reduction of machines and suspension of work in various silk weaving factories. Silk sales are sluggish. Last weekend, raw silk factory sales stagnated and silk prices plunged. Grade A was only 3.4 dollars per pound, Grade B 2.9 dollars, and Grade C 2.4 dollars, a decrease of 0.2-0.3 American dollars.

Tea Market Is Unusually Quiet

Yesterday, the tea market in this port was quite quiet. Duder Yongxing Jinlong and other firms were slightly interested in high-quality Zhenmei tea, but sales were very low. There were no major transactions in Zhenmei and Xiumei tea. The market was very depressed.

Piece Goods: Fine Twill Rises the Most

Eastern Goods Revive Due to the Rise in Exchange Rates

Western Goods, such as Yuan Velvet, Are Also Moving

Local Cotton Cloth: The market has seen mixed ups and downs in recent days. Fine cloth has softened slightly. Yesterday, Blue Double Fish and Color Ball were both sold for 6.95 taels. Yang He was sold for 6.925 taels. Jixiang has no spot goods due to the ongoing strike at the Rihua Factory. The demand for Blue Flying Fish from Qinhuangdao is strong. There are no spot goods even at 7.3 taels. Fine twill is rising sharply. The street is actively searching for it, leading to new high prices for various brands. Yang He sold for 7.075 taels, Blue Double Fish for 6.875 taels, and Jincheng for 6.925 taels. The trend of coarse cloth is stable. 16-pound Five Cranes is still 7.2 taels, Double Elephant is 7 taels, 14-pound Feeding Horse has no goods, and 11-pound cloth is 4.7 taels.

Eastern and Western Piece Goods: Due to the recent rise in exchange rates, the market has become more active. Eastern goods rose yesterday. Straight Gongduan was up 0.025 taels, the First Merit was 2.9 taels, Four Scholars had no goods, Magpie Bridge Meeting was 2.7 taels, and Jiaoye Title Book was 2.675 taels. The rise in Straight Gongne was even stronger. Sima Xiangru now requires 3.4 taels, Santan 3.35 taels. Changbanqiao, which has been out of stock for a long time, has arrived and opened at 3.3 taels. Double Child Deer sold for 2.65 taels. The Four Gentlemen produced by local and foreign factories sold for 2.425 taels yesterday. New pattern Straight Gongne color Zigong flower velvet is very active on this street. More than 100 pieces were sold yesterday. Western goods, such as Chongxi Duan, rose by 0.01 tael. Sassoon Tianguan sold for 3.4 taels, and Fair Nine Money Boy sold out at 3.35 taels. Only Six Yuan Velvet has recovered slightly.

Hardware: Black Iron Sheet Transactions Reach 500-600 Bundles

The black iron sheet market has seen gradually increasing demand from northern traders lately. Yesterday, 500-600 bundles were sold. The purchasers were all from Tianjin, Yantai, and Dalian. It is said that traders from Niuzhuang and Yingkou also made some purchases. There is not much spot goods on the market. Prices may rise later. Currently, 3x6 feet are estimated at 9 taels, and 2x6 feet opened at 10.05 taels.
